  6. I'm was a habitual shaver by default. I've tried all forms of wax from home versions to professional and every form of cream. All have left me disappointed and still with leg hair. Now I will admit that I have some thick and dark hair on parts of my legs that can only be removed by shaving. I hate razors because it's expensive and full of nicks, oops's and patches missed. I thought I would give an epilator a shot since it was the only thing I haven't tried. I'm happy I did!<br /><br />The device itself is awesome. The size is comfortable to handle and doesn't cramp your hand when used for long periods. There are 3 speeds: off, slow and fast. I like the fast setting just because you get the maximum hair pulling in the shortest time. It's a bit intense the first time you try it, but you'll quickly adjust. It's easy to maneuver between speeds and I wouldn't modify it at all. There is an intensely bright light above the speed settings. It could be used as a mini flashlight if need be. It makes it easy to see missed areas, short or baby soft hair. Not sure what I'm going to do when it stops working. The massage attachment is ok for beginning. It feels ok, but it doesn't get close enough to pull out those super short hairs. The non-massaging attachment is my best friend because it gets those barely there hairs. Both are easy to clean with the given brush and with water. The actual tweezing barrel can be a pain to clean with the brush so I just run it under water. The charging/low battery lights are in a good place and are easy to interpret. Give it plenty of time to charge the first time and charge it after each use or 40 minutes before the next use. It's battery life isn't outstanding, but it gets the job done. I'm not mad at it.<br /><br />Despite everything that's awesome about it, the noise it makes is deafening. It's a very loud device and while you get used to the noise, others might not. Be mindful on who's in the room or home when you useit.<br /><br />I'll be honest - it hurts, but not in a &#34;I'll never do it again&#34; kind of way. It's a strange sensation. On thick hair it hurts a lot and I ice my legs or underarms to numb the area. It's rather fast and satisfying to see those thick hairs hit the road. However, you'll never know how much baby hair you have until you clean the epilator. Those little fine hairs can take time to remove (it hurts much less, too!), so plan accordingly. If I can't do it in one day because of time, I'll do it over the course of a two days. If I can manage to do everything in one day, it feels like I'm getting tattoos all over again. Just irritating pain that feels like baby needles. Sounds painful and scary, but it's really not. It's just mind over matter.<br /><br />When you use it the first time expect general irritation and redness. Try it before bed just to give the unhappiness time to settle down. After that initial use, the irritation is minimal to non existent. Invest in a good lotion, exfoliant and emergency ingrown hair remedy. AmLactin is great for bumps and helps out on all three fronts. I hand make my scrubs to help things along as well. If I get an ingrown hair (it happens sometimes despite all the prevention) I use Prid salve.<br /><br />I'm not longer a slave to shaving and now it's 2 weeks before I consider my next hair removal session. I couldn't be happier!
  7. As a regular shaver, this was my first experience using an epilator. I was excited to try the Silk Epil 7 since I'm a mom of a busy toddler and would love to be able to cut showers shorter. I was also drawn to the convenience of being able to shave wet or dry. I was relieved that the process was less painful than I expected. Pain level and tolerance varies by individual, but for me it was reasonable given that the goal is to pull hair out by the roots. From the first I was able to do both legs dry with no problem. When I got brave and did a test on underarms I found that to be too painful. I'll stick with shaving underarms and other tender areas. I was also pleased that in a reasonable period of time the Silk Epil 7 did a good job of removing hair. My legs looked hairless, but didn't feel quite silky smooth. Every once in a while there seemed to a hair just long enough to feel but barely too short to remove. Nonetheless, I was satisfied. There's a lot to like about this epilator. The light helps make sure you're getting all the hairs with fewer passes. The massaging head is a nice touch, although I couldn't tell a large difference over the plain white head that's also included. The wipes are nice, but I'd be willing to continue using the epilator without buying more. There are also two speeds depending on your preference of being faster or gentler. While I could live without most of the features, they are nice. The massaging head, speed settings or wipes might make the difference for someone who's more on the fence about tolerating the pain of epilation. I did pinch myself using the unit once. I was using high speed, the plain head and perhaps applying a bit too much pressure while trying to get the last few hairs from my knees. It was painful (even compared to purposefully yanking your hair out!) and left a mark but didn't create a major injury or hurt for long. It's made me more cautious about applying too much pressure over uneven areas, but hasn't keptme from wanting to use it again. Another issue is that my legs were smooth for about a week after the first use, and then I noticed regrowth. Because it was about ¼ of the number of hairs I normally have, I assume those simply weren't grown in when I did the initial epilation. But of course if you go back and epilate those then you continue to have staggered hair growth. My guess is the solution is to make sure you've waited long enough since shaving so that all hairs are long enough to be plucked. I realize that this is probably an issue with epilation in general versus the Silk Epil 7 specifically, but something to think about if you're considering trying it. Update: I've tried this a few more times after waiting between epilating (went back to shaving for awhile, then waited for it hair to get long enough.) Again, my legs were smooth but I had a crop of hair grow in within the week. It was sparse but enough to need to shave. If I need to shave again within days, why use an epilator? I'm not sure if this problem is universal, and it probably has nothing to do with this particular model, but I don't find it worth the time and pain.

  16. Before the Braun Silk-&eacute;pil 7, I'd never used an epilator. That said, I have waxed (only a few times; hated it), and I pluck my eyebrows regularly -- so I'm no stranger to removing hair by the root. So far I've used the Silk-&eacute;pil twice on my legs, and I have to say that I really like it.<br /><br />What comes in the package: The epilator, two caps, a charger, a cinch pouch, a small flat cleaning brush, and a package of 16 Olay pre-epilation wipes. The epilator is cordless and has a rechargeable Li-ion battery, and it's totally waterproof -- so you can use it in the shower.<br /><br />One thing you can't see on the stock photo or the packaging is that a large portion of the epilator is glittery, underneath a smooth plastic coating. I don't consider myself a \\"girly\\" girl, but I absolutely love the glitter: it's fancy and happy and festive. I also adore the orange accents. Chalk it up to personal preference, but I feel like this epilator was practically designed for me.<br /><br />How to use it: You move/glide the epilator over your skin just like you would a razor or electric shaver. You don't have to press hard, but the epilation head (the rotating, tweezing cylinder) and the cap need to be touching your skin. The cap pivots, which is nice for going over curves.<br /><br />I opted not to use the pre-epilation wipes because of the ingredient list (I'm more of a natural-products person). I would guess that they have some sort of topical numbing agent in them, because it says to use them on your skin and then wait 30 minutes before epilating. They might be just the ticket for some people, but not for me personally. Plus, I wanted to see what the real deal was: I decided I'd either epilate \\"sober\\" or not at all.<br /><br />Frankly, I was terrified that it was going to hurt, and I had to psyche myself up before using it. I have a few small hairs at the bottom of my shin, so I decided to test the epilator there to see exactly how painful it would be. I told myself that if it didn't hurt too much, I would keep trying it on other areas; but if it was excruciating, well, at least the pain would be over quickly. So I put the epilator to my skin, and, surprisingly, it just felt like a few tiny, rapidfire pinpricks. I mean, yes, it hurt; but it wasn't nearly as bad as I expected, so I continued to use it and ended up doing both of my legs. My pain threshold is probably on the slightly higher side of normal (thanks to a relentlessly cruel monthly gift from mother nature), and I found that epilating different areas of my body hurt to different degrees. It hurt more to epilate my right leg than my left. And my knees hurt more than my shins. Surprisingly, the backs of my knees didn't hurt at all.<br /><br />As soon as I took the epilator off my skin, the pain stopped. So you have complete control over how long you want the acute pain to last. This may not happen with everyone, but I did get a slight endorphin rush to each area I had just epilated, much like what happens while you're getting a tattoo. Then I put on some lotion, and aside from the little red dots on my skin (which went away after about four hours), you'd never know I had just epilated.<br /><br />I used the vibrating massage cap, which is orange and has a set of textured rollers on either side of the epilation head. When the epilator is turned on, this cap really does vibrate, which helps distract your skin from the temporary pain. After an area has been effectively epilated (which you'll know because it stops hurting), the vibration actually feels really nice on your skin.<br /><br />Drawbacks:<br />- The buzzing sound the epilator makes is kind of loud. But every other small, motored device I've used has also been loud, so this probably can't be helped. Just know that this isn't the kind of thing you can use in the same room as someone who's sleeping, or even in the adjacent room with the door closed, because they'll still hear it.<br />-Yes, it hurts, especially if you've never used an epilator before. But it's not unbearable. For me, the pain was tolerable, and the end result was worth it. I intend to keep using it. I've been plucking my eyebrows since my teens, which hurt at first but doesn't anymore. I can only assume the pain will likewise subside with continued and consistent epilation.<br /><br />What helps reduce the pain?<br />- Epilating a little bit at a time, stopping for a few minutes and doing something else (reading, checking your email, doing other parts of your beauty routine, etc.), and then resuming a few minutes later. This helps to disperse the pain into more manageable increments.<br />- Doing shorter strokes instead of long ones. Run the epilator over your skin in the same way you would brush the short fur of a dog or cat (ever used a Furminator before?), pressing down momentarily with a short stroke, and then lifting the epilator back up almost immediately. This makes the epilation process take longer, but I find that it's far less painful to do little bits at a time. Once you've \\"cleared out\\" a larger area, then you can go back over it in one long, continuous stroke to get any remaining hairs.<br />- Remember to BREATHE. Take long, deep breaths. Unclench your jaw and relax your muscles. Just like when you're shaving, you can put yourself on \\"autopilot\\" when using the epilator and focus instead on making sure you're breathing deeply and relaxing your muscles.<br />- Although I haven't personally tried this, two of my friends who use epilators agree that drinking a glass of wine beforehand helps takes the edge off the pain. ;)<br />- One of those same friends also recommends singing while you epilate, so you have something else (positive!) to concentrate on as well as a kind of vocal catharsis for the pain.<br /><br />Cleaning the epilator is fairly easy. I was shocked at how many hairs had accumulated inside the cap. I had to spend several minutes running the epilation head under the faucet as I used the small brush (included) to clean out all the little hairs that were stuck in it. It was clean after about three minutes of thorough attention with the brush and flushing with water. For me, that wasn't too long to spend cleaning. I let it air-dry overnight and put it away the next morning.<br /><br />How long does the epilation last? Everyone's hair grows back at different rates, but this epilator says that you'll have smooth skin for 19 days. I'll come back and update my review when I've determined how long I can go between epilations. I did notice that, after about 3 days, there were some tiny hairs that the epilator either didn't get or that hadn't broken the skin at the time I epilated. It just took a few quick swipes to epilate these little fuzzies.<br /><br />All in all, I really like this epilator, and I will definitely keep using it. It beats shaving by a long shot!<br /><br />** Update, August 2, 2011 **<br /><br />I'm still using this epilator each week, and I have to say that it's awesome. My legs will stay totally smooth for about 48-72 hours, at which point a sparse \\"batch\\" of little hairs (from the previous week's epilation cycle) will start growing back in. Epilating once a week takes care of it. I've also found that, if you epilate regularly, it hurts less each time. This is because 1) you're probably getting desensitized to it, and 2) there are fewer individual hairs to pluck out each time because they all grow back at slightly different rates. So your first epilation is definitely the most painful, since you're not accustomed to the pain but you're also plucking out *all* the hairs in one go, instead of just a sparse batch each week.<br /><br />** Update, September 1, 2011 **<br /><br />I was cleaning my epilator a few days ago and saw through a pinhole that a bunch of hairs had jammed themselves up next to the gear-turning mechanism. The epilator was still working without a hitch, but it annoyed me that hairs could get trapped in a \\"sealed\\" compartment. The compartment is secured with two Torx (six-pointed star) screws, which are typically used in electronics that consumers aren't supposed to open (hard drives, mice, etc.). Being a resourceful woman, I have [[ASIN:B000MF754W this handy little screwdriver & bit set]] in my tool box and was able to use the T8 Torx bit to open the compartment. Then I was able to flush out all the trapped hairs and reassemble the epilator when everything was dry. An easy fix to a minor yet annoying design flaw, provided you have the right tools.<br /><br />** Update, August 31, 2012 **<br /><br />I'm still using my epilator! It's great. After almost a year and a half, it still holds a charge like a champ. After epilating exclusively (i.e., not shaving) my legs for several months, I noticed that I started getting tiny ingrown hairs that would simply not break the skin but either coil or lie flat right below the surface, forming little bumps. I realized I needed to exfoliate in combination with epilating, so I brought my razor back into the picture. The schedule that works best for me is if I epilate over the weekend and then shave my legs about mid-week. This has a dual purpose: 1) shaving mid-week keeps the new \\"batch\\" of hairs from getting terribly long before I epilate again, and 2) shaving also exfoliates the skin on my legs, thus preventing ingrown hairs.d under the faucet as I used the small brush (included) to clean out all the little hairs that were stuck in it.   29. Let me preface this review by saying that I am against the whole concept of an epilator that can be used in the shower or while the skin is wet. However, I had no luck finding a newer 'dry only' model of my previous Braun X'elle - this wet/dry version seemed to be the only game in town. I could have saved about twenty or thirty bucks if I'd found the old fashioned version, as this one pulls hairs with the same efficiency and precision as the previous model, yet costs signficantly more. The other argument to possibly justify the cost is that it's cordless, but again I would have preferred to save the money and stick with the corded version. Having epilated for three years, it has been my experience that the best way to ensure pulling hair at the root is to make sure skin is dry and taught, and of course being able to see exactly what you're doing helps a lot. Standing in the shower with slippery skin and running an epilator over it is a good way to miss hairs and/or break them in half. In light of that, the rest of this review pertains to dry usage only - I did not and will not use under water or with wet skin. This model is considerate to the needs of first-time epilators - those likeliest to experience pain with hair removal. Two different caps are included that fit over the tweezer element- one for beginners with the little roller heads on it to help lessen the pulling sensation - this looked to be more or less the same one that they were including with my older model X'elle, so no upgrade there. The other cap is for those with prior epilation experience who want to get the job done as quickly as possible. I would note to beginners here that although it may lessen the pain to start out with the beginner's cap and/or use this in the shower, don't be surprised if you wind up with a lot of missed or broken off hairs that don't come out at the root. What I would suggest to you first-timers who are afraid of the pain is to shave or wax first, wait 1 day to a week depending on your rate of hair growth, just until it's a bit stubbly, and start out on dry skin with the starter cap for the best traction and results. Keep an ice pack handy if you feel you will need it. (This one does not come with one btw, whereas my prior X'elle did). Being impervious to epilation pain on my lower legs and underarms at this point, the \\"pro\\" cap worked fine and I thought it moved along faster than my older model, but after using a couple of times I started to wonder why bother with any cap at all as it blocks some of the tweezers and creates an obstruction so that all tweezer heads do not come in contact with the skin. So I took the cap off and started epilating with the uncovered tweezer heads and found this thing can roll FAST! It swiftly glided over my legs and removed hairs so quickly and painlessly -- until I reached a spot where a stubborn hair wasn't coming out and I kept rolling over it. Long story short, don't try this at home! I skinned about 2 inches off my leg and won't be trying that again. Yes, the Braun does miss a couple of stubborn hairs that you have to keep going over but the vast majority get plucked out from the root and it is worlds better than the Emjoy at uprooting ingrowns. Before I purchased this I didn't realize it could only be used cordlessly. Which meant that some days I would have to plan ahead and recharge in advance, instead of just plugging in and using it whenever I felt like it. I also didn't like the idea of having to worry about the battery dying midway through, but I have to say the charge lasted long enough for me to do both lower legs and then some (I usually don't bother with the upper legs..prefer to shave or wax there) and it recharges fairly quickly. I also am finding that I use it more often as I enjoy the flexibilty and ease of use of a cordless model. All in all, I really like the device and would give it 3.5 stars - when used properly with a cap over the tweezer heads - it is totally painless and efficient. However I don't think the price is justified as it tweezes just as well as the older models at a higher price point. Braun should bring those back - they are hard to find and I don't know if they are still making them. Another issue with Braun is that they list their current models on their website with one name and they are sold under another, making it very difficult to figure out which product you're actually buying and what features it has in it. For example the Xpressive that's documented on the Braun website is marketed as the Silk Epil 7 everywhere else. Amazon is one of the few websites that uses both names in the product description so you know what product you're getting, and that's how I finally figured it out.

Some quick thoughts on this model specifically:<br />* Removes smaller hairs than earlier models, so you can be more aggressive as stray hairs start to grow back<br />* The \\"massagers\\" on the epilation head really do help<br />* You can use it dry or completely-wet, but not damp (e.g., right after the shower won't work)<br />* You can't use it while plugged in (that would be a serious safety hazard in the shower! but it means that whenever the battery eventually stops holding a charge, you'll have to toss the unit)<br />* I wish it included a trimming head, for the cases when you have longer hairs you want to attack (they have to be 1 cm or shorter before this will really pull them out)<br />* The small spotlight on the unit makes it much easier to see hairs you may have missed<br />* The wipes really do help. You'll use one and think it didn't help that much, then try the other leg without one at all, and realize it WAS helping more than you realized :) I used them the first time I epilated, but haven't bothered subsequently.<br />* Update: after a year or two of using this item, the cap pops off while you're using it, which is seriously annoying. But I love it apart from that.<br /><br />And some thoughts on epilation in general:<br />* This seems obvious, but I have to say it: it only hurts when a hair is being removed. This means that the first time you epilate, it's very uncomfortable. But since only a small percentage of the hair later grows back, the subsequent touch-ups really aren't bad at all, especially on your legs. (Underarms are less comfortable, and bikini area even less so.)<br />* The first time you epilate, your legs will be unbelievably smooth. But hair grows back at different rates, so after a month or so of epilating (maybe one time each week), you'll have tiny hairs here and there, that are starting to grow back, but are still too small to get. It's less of an issue with this epilator than others, and the hairs aren't really visible. So if youthink someone's going to be touching your legs, then shave :-D but otherwise life is much easier if you just epilate once a week or so. Then if you don't bother doing anything for a month or so, you'll have a few stray hairs here and there, but nothing like someone who shaves regularly and then skips a month (or even a week... or even 3 days). Visible stubble is entirely a thing of the past.<br />* You do have to use a loofah or some other type of exfoliation on your legs occasionally to prevent ingrown hairs (just little bumps on your legs--mine don't turn red). But if you wax, or if you age ;) you'll have to do that anyway<br />* And how could I forget the #1 reason to epilate: no more underarm bumps. You know, the ones that you ALWAYS have, despite a million products on the market that say they'll banish them but don't? Sometimes when you epilate, your skin will be red for 30-90 seconds afterward, but then it fades. So NO MORE BUMPS. That alone is reason enough to own an epilator, IMO :)

  98. I've only used corded epilators before. I thought they're more powerful and last longer than rechargebles. I had an old Braun one for 5 years. No one was selling my old Braun epilator and that's why I looked at this one. I love it. I run it on top speed for best performance.<br />Pros:<br />1)The rechargeable battery lasts a long time. I've gone weeks without a single recharge.<br />2)It's just as powerful as my old corded one<br />3)I love the light. It's bright and I can spot places I've missed.<br />4)My body has been silky smooth for a week before I notice any hair growth.<br /><br />There are really no cons, but I believe people list cons due to their inexperience.<br />Cons:<br />1) It hurts: That's because they've never used an epilator before. Well, yes, it hurts more than shaving because shaving just doesn't hurt at all. There's going to be a certain amount of pain when you are pulling out hair. It hurts a lot less then tweezing and feel similar to waxing. Don't let the hair get longer than 1/4 inch before epilating. Use a scissor and cut it down first. Otherwise you'll get hair that's broken instead of being pulled out and that hurts. The longer and thicker the hair, the more painful it'll be because like all epilators, it can't grab long thick hair well. Reduce that by not letting the hair get so long. You can also use lidocaine cream before epilating as that will numb the area and help with sensitive areas. Body parts, legs being least sensitive to armpits to your groin which will be most sensitive. For legs and armpits, follow along the hair pattern. For groin, go perpendicular to the hair for best pick up and least pain. The pain actually decreases as you use it more often and more frequently. Wet epilating is less painful than dry. I don't feel pain, but there's apparently a lot of sensitive people out there. Also once you've epilated a spot, you'll notice no pain because no hair is being pulled out from that spot. You can also test how hard you can push the epilator on that spot and notice no pain, no skin grab. Don't be lazy and let the hair grow out so long and then complain it hurts because you didn't follow directions.<br />2)skin grabbing: When epilating, press the rotating part against your skin. Don't let it loosely touch your skin. If you have areas you can easily pinch, that means the skin there is loose. Pull it taunt before epilating. Like vacuuming a rug. If you do not pull the rug taunt, the vacuum will pull the rug into it. Very few people have loose skin, that's why you don't hear many complaints about skin pulling. People get scared and let it lightly touch the skin. That's bad because the epilator can't grab the hair correctly and will cause pain.<br />2)I get ingrown hairs: When the hairs are too long or you are not making sure the epilator is on your skin when epilating, you get hair breakage. Basically the hair is not being completely pulled out. Instead it's broken with the roots still in the body. So the hair can still grow, but changes it's growth pattern. Thus you get ingrown hair. Solution for it again is to cut the hair short to 1/4 inch before epilating. Also make sure the epilator is pressing on your skin.<br />3)I'm breaking out in the areas I've epilated: You need to make sure the area is clean before epilating. Best after soaping during a shower or just after a shower. If it's not clean, bacteria, dirt, and other things get in the areas where the hair has been removed.<br />4)Poor battery life: I've had my epilator for a year now, no problems. Could be a manufacturer defect if it dies before a year. Prolong your battery life by letting it die before doing a full charge. Don't half charge, use it, half charge.<br />Hope this helps.

Obviously I can't speak to how many charges this device will hold, so I can't take off any stars for that. If you want it to last longer however, you'll want to deplete the charge fully every once in a while before recharging it again.<br /><br />IF YOU'RE NEW TO EPILATION, expect some initial pain during the removal process. There's just no way around it outside of a glass of wine or some ibuprofen. You'll need to epilate every few days at first if you're a shaver--waxers should be able to switch over with ease. Here's why: human hair grows in cycles--of the millions of hair follicles on your legs, some are active and some are not. To complicate matters more, of the active ones, they're all in different stages of growth--which means some will hurt like the dickens when you pull them out by the roots, while others will come out willingly with little to no pain. The only solution to this is to power through and continue epilating regularly. Eventually you'll only be pulling out the same set of hairs from active follicles, and it will hurt a lot less (but it will still hurt, sorry).<br /><br />IF YOU'RE BRAVE enough to try bikini/underarm epilation, try the [[ASIN:B0016GTOHC Braun SE7781 Silk-Epil Xpressive Epilator Body System, Rechargeable]], which comes with the underarm/bikini trimmer cap and a shaving foil.he battery may eventually wear out and not be able to hold a charge. Also, as you can imagine, the sparser the hair the more tolerable the pain. So I anticipate that each subsequent hair removal will hurt less because you will only be catching one growth cycle at a time. (and incredibly soft). As with waxes, I expect some hairs to start growing back in a couple of days (at which point I will use the Silk Epil to pull them back out!)<br /><br />SUMMARY<br /><br />Silk Epil was realtively easy to use and quite effective at pulling out hair. Despite the surprising amount of pain, I will definitely be keeping up the epilation for my arms and legs as it's WAY cheaper than going to get them waxed and I can tolerate the pain. However, for sensitive regions, like underarms and bikini, I will continue getting professional waxes.
